The behavior is not pure principle (that would be sublimation/altruism); there is a defensive component — the reaction formation against being-her-mother, being-her-father, being-her-sister.

Observable signs:
- The shingle is deliberately shabby. The car is a beater. The wardrobe is curated thrift.
- When wealth becomes tactically useful she will use it (she has financed operations), but she requires the operational justification; she will not use it for comfort alone.
- The cleanest test case: she has refused Bishop money repeatedly when accepting it would have eased material suffering — the LA arc demonstrates a willingness to **eat genuine deprivation rather than touch tainted resources.**

This is the most visible neurotic defense in her file. It is not yet costly enough to flag as pathology but it is the structure most likely to mellow with age — predicted trajectory is that she will, in her thirties, accept a more comfortable baseline without losing her ethical center.

---

### 7.9 ISOLATION OF AFFECT — Narrow, Family-of-Origin Zone

She can speak about Derek Bishop's criminality in flat, near-clinical register. The affect is sequestered. This is partly adaptive (she could not function otherwise) and partly evasive (the rage has not been fully processed and surfaces only obliquely, in the precision of the contempt she reserves for him).

The isolation is much weaker around her mother (§7.13). The Eleanor zone is where her defenses are least clean.

---

### 7.10 DENIAL — Localized, Eleanor-Specific

The single recurring failure of reality-testing in an otherwise reality-grounded operative. Each cycle is the same: Eleanor returns; offers a softer story; Kate upgrades trustworthiness on insufficient evidence; reality reasserts; Kate is briefly destabilized; Kate restores. This is **selective denial** in the technical sense — the rest of her judgment is intact, but in this one zone the want overrides the evidence.

Importantly, the denial is **time-limited.** It does not become a delusional structure. She updates, eventually, every cycle. The defense is therefore better classified as a *recurring transient denial* than as a fixed cognitive distortion.

---

### 7.11 SPLITTING — Functionally Absent, Brief Echo Only

She does not split. Her relationships are stable, her self-concept is integrated, she tolerates ambivalence well. Steve Rogers can be right and wrong; Clint can be magnificent and infuriating; Eleanor can be loved and condemned. The Bishop file is largely free of all-good/all-bad alternations.

The one echo is the **bright-line cut** with Derek Bishop — but this is not splitting (which would require oscillation); it is a *settled* moral judgment after sufficient evidence. The defense functions correctly because the data warrants the verdict.

---

### 7.12 ACTING-OUT — Almost Absent

This is the diagnostically interesting negative. A trauma survivor whose defenses had not matured would be expected to show some acting-out: substance use, risky sexual behavior, self-injury, reckless escalation. Subject shows none of these. The closest behavioral analog is **counter-phobic risk taking** in operational contexts — running toward fights — but this is channeled through training and team structure, and it is not impulsive. It is the inverse of acting-out: it is acting *through*.

---

### 7.13 PRIMARY COMPENSATORY STRUCTURES — Positive

The *built* substitutes for what the family of origin did not provide. These are not defenses in the Vaillant sense; they are the architecture defenses sit on.

- **The codename.** Hawkeye is an earned, externally ratified identity that replaces "daughter of Derek Bishop." Steve Rogers' bestowal of the name in YA #11 is the institutional moment, but the identity is hers because she trained for it. Functions as a continuous reminder of agency.
- **The bow.** Tool, not totem. Distance, precision, deniable lethality, daily ritual. Replaces the helplessness of the assault with a literal extension of will across space.
- **Hawkeye Investigations.** A vocation she founded and operates. Replaces inherited position with earned position. The shingle is the structural answer to "who am I if not a Bishop."
- **The Young Avengers / WCA chosen family.** Replaces the family of origin. Tested by task, not by blood. Mutual, durable, articulated.
- **The dog (Lucky).** Specifically: a relationship with no power asymmetry to exploit, no betrayal capacity, and a daily ritual of care. For survivors, animals often carry disproportionate load; for her, Lucky is the place uncomplicated affection lives.
- **The geography (Venice / LA).** A deliberate continent of distance from the Bishop apparatus in Manhattan. Geographic compensation for psychological proximity.

Each structure is **independently load-bearing.** If any one were removed she would absorb the loss; if three were removed simultaneously the architecture would strain.

---

### 7.14 NEGATIVE / COSTLY COMPENSATIONS

- **Counter-dependency.** Difficulty accepting help, particularly material help. The cost is real: she has gone hungry, gone unhoused-adjacent, gone untreated for injuries that would have been better triaged. The defense protects against the specific terror of being-owned-by-a-Bishop and over-generalizes to all assistance.
- **Rescuer dynamic with Clint.** The most clinically interesting feature of her interpersonal life. She is drawn to a depressive older partner whose competence she partially carries. The reverse-parentification structure provides her with consistent altruism-yield, with identification material, and with a relationship in which she is never the wounded one — which is itself a defense against being the wounded one. The cost is borne when his crises eclipse her own needs and she does not register the imbalance.
- **The Eleanor reopening.** Already cataloged at §7.10. The compensation here is a *hope structure* — keeping the door open is the way she preserves the possibility of having had a mother. Closing it would finalize a loss she has not yet been willing to mourn.
- **Grandiosity-tinged impatience with first-meeting condescension.** A defended sore spot. When called "kid," "rich girl," or "the new Hawkeye" she works harder, shoots tighter, takes a risk she would otherwise pass on. The defense protects the earned identity from being demoted to inherited; it is exploitable by any adversary patient enough to provoke it.
- **Suppression-stacking under chronic stress.** When operational tempo is sustained, the suppression valve loads faster than humor and training can discharge it. Symptoms: snappishness with Clint specifically, shortened sleep, increased coffee, decreased delegation. She does not collapse — but the architecture is observably under load.

---

### 7.15 DEFENSIVE STACK BY RANK

Approximate hierarchy by frequency-of-use and load-bearing weight:

1. **Sublimation** (foundational)
2. **Altruism** (co-primary)
3. **Anticipation** (daily operational)
4. **Humor** (daily affective)
5. **Suppression** (situational, disciplined)
6. **Identification (selective)** (structural, parenting-substitute)
7. **Intellectualization** (trauma-localized)
8. **Reaction formation** (class-specific)
9. **Isolation of affect** (Derek-zone)
10. **Denial (transient)** (Eleanor-zone only)
11. **Splitting** (vestigial / absent)
12. **Acting-out** (vestigial / absent)

The top six carry roughly ninety percent of the daily defensive load. The bottom six are either zone-specific or vestigial. This is, in clinical terms, the profile of a **mature defensive organization with two narrow neurotic pockets and no primitive baseline.** It is the architecture of someone who got hurt, decided what kind of person she was going to be about it, and built the apparatus to be that person on purpose — and then maintained it, daily, for the entire span of her published life.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: KATE BISHOP

*Decade-by-decade clinical mapping, derived from canonical behavioral record (Young Avengers 2005 → present). Each stratum tracks four parameters: affect regulation, cognitive style, self-concept, and defensive organization, with attention to the *vectors of change* between strata.*

---

## STRATUM I — PRE-INDEX (childhood, ages ~6–15; reconstructed from later canon and flashback material)

**Affect regulation.** The earliest accessible data point — the "Hawkingbird" childhood nickname, glimpsed in flashback sequences and referenced obliquely across Heinberg and Thompson — points to a child who was already orienting toward a fantasy of competent rescue. The household, as later reconstructed, was affectively cold: Derek performatively warm, structurally absent; Eleanor "dead" or, in the revised history, performing death as a strategic exit; Susan, the older sister, modeling a feminine adaptation (compliance, marriage-track, social register) that the subject visibly rejected. The pre-trauma child's affect regulation was likely **externally scaffolded by domestic staff and routine** — there is a recurring tell in adult Kate's behavior of treating service-workers (drivers, doormen, the building super in the LA arc, baristas) with a familiarity warmer than she shows family; this is the residue of who actually raised her.

**Cognitive style.** Pre-trauma: precocious, observational, verbally fluent. The class register of her humor — Manhattan-private-school cadence, literary references that surface in stress, e.g. her habit of quipping in complete sentences mid-fight — locates the substrate. She was being educated for cultural capital.

**Self-concept.** Embryonic, family-defined, already destabilized by Eleanor's "death." The Hawkingbird nickname is the artifact of a child who had begun to construct an alternative self before she had a reason to need one.

**Defensive organization.** Age-appropriate. No data for pathology pre-index.

---

## STRATUM II — POST-INDEX ADOLESCENCE (ages ~15–18; Central Park assault through pre–Young Avengers)

This is the **constitutive period.** Everything downstream is shaped here.

**Affect regulation.** The acute post-assault picture is not directly depicted but is reconstructable from negative space: the subject does not present, in any later canon, with the dysregulation signatures common to untreated adolescent sexual assault — no eating-disorder history, no self-injury record, no substance-onset, no school-failure arc, no promiscuity-as-reenactment, no dissociative phenomena in later text. What we see instead is **a rapid, deliberate channeling of arousal into skill-acquisition** within months of the index event. By the time she appears in Young Avengers #1 she has functional competence in archery, jiu-jitsu, kickboxing, fencing, and swordsmanship — this is years of disciplined training, executed during the developmental window when most assault-survivors are decompensating. The clinical reading: she found, or someone found for her, a regulation strategy (physical mastery) early enough that the trauma was *metabolized in motion* rather than encysted in avoidance.

**Cognitive style.** Sharpens into the recognizable adult pattern: tactical, observational, prone to threat-modeling environments on entry. The "exits, weapons, allies" scan that later becomes professional is laid down here as **post-traumatic situational awareness, not yet operationalized.** Frame: Janoff-Bulman's *shattered assumptions* — the just-world belief and the personal-invulnerability belief are both destroyed; what replaces them is not nihilism but an **earned-vigilance worldview** in which safety is producible through preparation.

**Self-concept.** Under reconstruction. The "rich girl from the Upper East Side" identity is no longer tenable; the "victim" identity is being actively refused. The Hawkingbird fantasy resurfaces as a usable scaffold. This is the period in which the **counter-phobic project** is born: not "I am someone who was hurt" but "I am someone who is becoming someone who cannot be hurt this way again." Erikson would locate this as a foreclosed-into-achieved identity move executed under traumatic pressure.

**Defensive organization.** **Sublimation comes online as primary defense** — the developmental achievement of this stratum. Humor is being developed in parallel as a secondary register (her wit in YA #1 is already adult-grade, which is impossible without years of practice). Intellectualization begins — she is already, by the time we meet her, narrating the trauma to herself as *curriculum*.

---

## STRATUM III — EARLY YOUNG AVENGERS (ages ~18–20; Heinberg 2005 → Civil War → Children's Crusade)

**Affect regulation.** First period of observable functioning. The signature is **action-as-regulation**: when distressed, she moves, plans, equips. The wedding-crisis self-insertion in YA #1 is the prototypical Kate behavior — anxiety converted instantly into intervention. Notable absence: she does not freeze, does not cry, does not seek reassurance. She also does not rage; the affect is *cool execution under arousal*, which is the autonomic signature of someone who has trained the sympathetic surge to land on motor planning rather than panic. Recovery from acute stressors is fast — within scenes, not arcs.

**Cognitive style.** **Concrete-tactical with high pattern recognition** is now stable. She reads the team dynamics in YA #1–4 faster than the team reads itself; she correctly identifies who will hold and who will fold. Social cognition is her strongest cognitive zone — she is a natural Theory-of-Mind operator, which becomes the substrate of the later PI vocation.

**Self-concept.** *Choosing* the name "Hawkeye" before being given it is the central self-concept act of this stratum. She does not wait for permission; she takes the title and then earns it retroactively. Captain America's ratification in YA #11 closes the loop. From this point forward, she will never again be in identity-question with respect to her vocational self. The internal narrative — *I was hurt, I refused to stay hurt, I built a self around protecting* — is fully composed by age twenty.

**Defensive organization.** Mature-skewed and stabilizing. Sublimation primary, humor reliable, anticipation operational, altruism emergent (team-leadership begins here). The Eli Bradley romance is the first observable data point on the **low-stakes romance** pattern — affectionate but not load-bearing, ended without crisis when ended.

**Vector of change from Stratum II → III:** consolidation. The trauma-conversion strategy invented in adolescence is field-tested and works. She does not relapse to the index trauma under combat stress. The hypothesis that mastery-as-coping was the right intervention is confirmed by repeated exposure to genuine danger.

---

## STRATUM IV — INTERREGNUM AND LOS ANGELES (ages ~20–23; Fraction/Aja era, 2012–2015)

The **stress-test stratum.** Kate leaves New York, leaves the Bishop money, and lives the experiment of whether the self she constructed can sustain itself unsubsidized.

**Affect regulation.** Tested and confirmed. The Madame Masque arc — including a severe beating in Fraction #14–15 — produces no decompensation. She is alone, broke, in physical pain, in over her head, and she does not call for extraction. She does not call Clint until the case is closed. The signature is **autonomous self-soothing through task-completion**: she regulates by working the problem. This is when the adult affect profile crystallizes into its mature form — broad tolerance band, fast recovery, low baseline reactivity, anger expressed verbally and tactically, sadness brief and private. The drinking pattern noted across this period — social, never escalating, never used to incapacity — sets the negative control against Clint's depressive pattern and confirms she is not using substance regulation.

**Cognitive style.** Investigative cognition matures. She can now sit with **incomplete information** for arcs at a time without forcing premature closure — a developmental achievement. The PI work demonstrates a willingness to be wrong, to revise hypotheses, and to follow evidence where it leads even when it leads to her own family. The cognitive pattern is closer to *naturalistic decision-making* (Klein) than to formal analysis — she runs on pattern-matched intuition refined by feedback, not on Bayesian deliberation.

**Self-concept.** **Refused-inheritance identity** is the headline. She could call her father, get a loft, get a car, get an office. She does not. The self-concept now requires *material proof* — she is who she says she is only if she can pay the rent on it. This is the period in which her self-concept becomes **load-bearing under material adversity**, which is the strongest possible test. The risk of this strategy is mild counter-dependency, and that trait crystallizes here.

**Defensive organization.** Altruism becomes structural — the produce-for-services PI model is sublimation and altruism fused into a business model. Humor deepens, dries out, becomes the recognizable adult register. **Mild reaction-formation around wealth** is now stable: she performs scrappiness slightly harder than the situation requires, because she is fighting her own pull toward the easy option.

**The Clint dynamic begins here.** This is when the **rescuer-pattern with a beloved depressive** is laid down. The role-reversal — the younger woman as the functional adult, the older mentor as the disaster — is established in this stratum and becomes a permanent feature of her interpersonal life. Clinically, this is the most worth-watching pattern in her file because it has the structure of a chosen reenactment: she takes care of a competent-but-collapsing adult in the way the Bishop adults did not take care of her, and she gets to be the one who shows up. It is functional, mostly mutual, and stable, but it is the closest thing she has to a compulsion.

**Vector of change from III → IV:** individuation. The team-derived identity of the Young Avengers stratum is replaced by a sole-practitioner identity that does not require collective scaffolding.

---

## STRATUM V — VENICE BEACH / WCA / EARLY ADULT MASTERY (ages ~23–26; Thompson solo, West Coast Avengers, 2016–2019)

**Affect regulation.** The most regulated period in the record. She runs a business, a team, an apartment, a dog-adjacent social life, and a romantic life of light entanglements, all simultaneously. The affect profile is *broad-band stable* — she handles a Madame Masque return, the mother-villain revelation, the WCA roster's interpersonal chaos (a roster that includes Gwenpool and Kid Omega, both of whom would dysregulate most leaders), and her father's full criminal exposure, without affective collapse. The Eleanor revelation does produce a brief, private dysregulation — she goes quiet, withdraws to the apartment, drinks somewhat more than usual, and does not perform okay-ness — which is itself a sign of *health*, not pathology: she neither dissociates the affect nor acts it out, she *feels it briefly and privately and then organizes counter-action*.

**Cognitive style.** **Middle-manager-of-chaos cognition** matures. She demonstrates a leadership-cognitive style closer to Hersey-Blanchard situational leadership than to charismatic command: she calibrates her register to each team member — directive with Quentin, supportive with Gwen, peer-mode with America, light-touch with Clint. She is not a strategist; she is a *people-router* who knows what each operator does best and gets them aligned. This is the cognitive signature of someone who has read every person in the room and assigned them the work they can actually do.

**Self-concept.** *Stable, articulated, congruent.* The internal narrative is now narrated to others — she can describe her own arc when asked. The self-concept is robust enough that she no longer needs to defend it; she can be called "rich girl" and not bite, most of the time. The remaining sore spot — being condescended to on first meeting — is now a recognized vulnerability she can sometimes regulate around and sometimes cannot. The mother-revelation does not destabilize the self-concept; she absorbs *Eleanor is the villain* into the existing narrative (*the world contains real predators, including the one who raised me*) without identity collapse.

**Defensive organization.** Mature-skewed, with one persistent **selective-denial pocket**: Eleanor's redeemability. The cognitive error is small, isolated, and clinically interesting because it is so out of pattern — Kate's lie-detection is excellent in every other domain. The frame is **trauma-coherent attachment hunger**: she will keep reopening the door with her mother not because she misjudges Eleanor but because she cannot quite stop wanting a mother. This is mature insight; she knows she is doing it and does it anyway, which is the human signature rather than a pathological one.

**Vector of change IV → V:** integration. The Los Angeles experiment of unsubsidized adult selfhood is generalized into a life — a business, a team, a place, a network. She is no longer proving the self; she is operating it.

---

## STRATUM VI — A-LIST CONTEXT AND LATE-TWENTIES CONSOLIDATION (ages ~26+; Aaron Avengers, Ewing, Hickman-era and current)

**Affect regulation.** **Peer-level regulation in Captain-America-grade rooms.** She is now placed in contexts with Thor, Captain America, Carol Danvers, and operates without deference-anxiety or starstruck flutter. This is the **broadest-band stable** phase of the file. The only consistent disorganizers remain narrow: Eleanor, Clint-under-threat, the chosen family writ large.

**Cognitive style.** **Practical intelligence at full operational capacity.** She is not a Reed-Richards abstract; she is not a Steve-Rogers grand-strategist; she is the operator who reads the room, reads the mission, reads the people, and executes. The cognitive style has stopped developing in *kind* and is now developing in *range* — she handles bigger problems with the same tools.

**Self-concept.** **Earned, congruent, and increasingly transferable.** She mentors. She is sought. She is now, herself, the kind of figure she once needed — and her behavior toward younger recruits across this stratum (protective, developmental, undermining of pedestals) suggests she knows this and is deliberate about it. The "kid who the team didn't want" memory is now operationalized as **trauma-informed mentorship** rather than residue.

**Defensive organization.** Mature defenses dominant and stable. The Eleanor-pocket is still there. The Clint rescuer-pattern is still there, possibly slightly softening as Clint has been written into his own functional stretches. The counter-dependency around material help has not resolved and probably will not — it is now a personality feature rather than a symptom.

**Vector V → VI:** transmission. What she built for herself, she now teaches.

---

## CROSS-STRATUM PARAMETERS — THE LONG ARCS

**Affect regulation — overall vector:** *Adolescent counter-phobic action-channeling* (II) → *combat-tested cool execution* (III) → *autonomous self-soothing through task* (IV) → *broad-band stable across domains* (V) → *peer-level regulation in elite contexts* (VI). The arc is **monotonic improvement with no relapse**, which is itself a rare clinical finding and the single strongest argument for the post-traumatic-growth reading.

**Cognitive style — overall vector:** *Precocious observational* (I) → *post-traumatic situational scanning* (II) → *tactical-with-pattern-recognition* (III) → *investigative-with-tolerance-for-incomplete-information* (IV) → *people-routing-managerial* (V) → *practical intelligence at full operational range* (VI). The arc is **additive, not transformative** — she keeps acquiring layers without discarding earlier capacities. The Manhattan-private-school verbal substrate is still audible in the late-stratum quips; the post-trauma threat-scan is still operating under the A-list missions; the LA-PI evidence-discipline is still working when she leads.

**Self-concept — overall vector:** *Family-defined and destabilizing* (I) → *under-reconstruction-from-the-victim-position* (II) → *chosen-and-ratified-vocational* (III) → *materially-proven-and-refused-inheritance* (IV) → *narratable-to-others* (V) → *earned-and-transmissible* (VI). The arc is **the rarest pattern in the genre**: a legacy hero who never has a *who am I really* arc after the founding one, because the founding act resolved the question with finality. She does not crisis-quit. She does not unname. She does not lose the bow and have to find herself. The self-concept work was front-loaded in adolescence and the rest of the life has been *operating* the answer.

**Defensive organization — overall vector:** Sublimation-primary throughout, with humor, anticipation, altruism, and intellectualization layering in across strata. Mild reaction-formation around wealth (IV onward) and selective denial around Eleanor (V onward) are the only persistent immature-defense residues, and both are narrow, recognized, and non-spreading. The defensive picture is best summarized as **maturely defended with two named exceptions she knows about.**

---

## CLINICAL SUMMARY OF THE LONGITUDINAL PICTURE

Kate Bishop's twenty-year published life maps as a single, coherent post-traumatic growth trajectory, executed with unusual cleanness for the genre. The constitutive trauma was metabolized in adolescence via mastery-channeling within the developmental window that allowed it to become identity rather than wound. Each subsequent stratum has been an **expansion of operating range** without alteration of the underlying structure. She did not change who she was; she enlarged what she could do as that person. The two persistent vulnerabilities — Eleanor and Clint — are not pathologies but *the price of having retained the capacity to want a mother and to love a damaged mentor*, which is to say, the price of not having armored too well. The clinical picture is, end-to-end, **a survivor whose coping was effective and remained so**, and the longitudinal record is the documentation of that effectiveness compounding.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — KATHERINE ELIZABETH BISHOP

*Classification: Subject is a non-enhanced civilian operative with a documented index trauma, a sustained high-risk vocation, and approximately two decades of observable behavioral record across published canon. This section integrates DSM-5-TR and ICD-11 analog frameworks; where the genre context (superhuman environment, sliding-scale chronology, narrative compression) distorts standard clinical timelines, the distortion is named. The assessment is independent and built from the behavioral evidence, not from any character's self-report.*

---

## 1. PRIMARY DIAGNOSTIC IMPRESSION

### 1.1 Posttraumatic Stress Disorder, Partial Remission, with Predominant Hypervigilance and Post-Traumatic Growth (DSM-5-TR 309.81 / ICD-11 6B40, partial)

**Index trauma.** Sexual assault, adolescence, Central Park, perpetrator unidentified. The event meets Criterion A unambiguously: actual sexual violence, directly experienced, in a context where the subject was unprotected and outnumbered. The assault is referenced in *Young Avengers* #3 with deliberate authorial restraint, confirmed across Fraction/Aja's *Hawkeye* run and the Thompson solo titles, and reflected in the subject's earliest self-disclosure to Cassie Lang — a disclosure framed not as confession but as explanation for the training.

**Criterion-by-criterion behavioral mapping.**

- **Criterion B (Intrusion).** Minimal observable signature. No documented flashbacks. No documented nightmares disclosed in narrative voice. No dissociative re-experiencing in canon. The closest behavioral analog is a startle-suppression pattern: the subject reacts to sudden close-range physical approach with a micro-reorientation (weight shift to rear foot, hands rising to mid-line, breath held one beat) that is too fast to be cognitive and too consistent to be coincidence. This is *residual* intrusion encoded somatically rather than cognitively. Sub-threshold for an active intrusion criterion.

- **Criterion C (Avoidance).** Strikingly absent in the modalities one would expect. The subject does not avoid Central Park (operates there freely), does not avoid being alone at night (lives alone, walks at night, conducts surveillance at night), does not avoid male company (mentor, romantic partners, team members), does not avoid the topic when raised by trusted persons. There is one narrow avoidance: she will not be in a position of physical helplessness *without a planned exit.* This is not phobic avoidance; it is operationalized avoidance — converted into a logistical preference. Sub-threshold.

- **Criterion D (Negative alterations in cognition and mood).** Largely absent. The subject does not exhibit the depressive-cognitive triad common to chronic PTSD. She does not describe herself as damaged, broken, contaminated, or culpable. She is not detached from others — her attachment behavior is in fact more robust than baseline. Anhedonia is absent. The single mild residual is a moderately negativistic *world-belief schema*: predators are real, institutions fail, you handle it yourself. This belief is reality-tested and partially correct given her operational environment; it is not the catastrophizing of acute PTSD but the calibrated cynicism of someone who has been right to be wary. Sub-threshold for criterion D as a pathological process.

- **Criterion E (Alterations in arousal and reactivity).** This is where the residue lives. Hypervigilance is present, persistent, and structurally embedded in the subject's vocation, equipment, spatial behavior, and sleep architecture. She scans rooms on entry. She maps egress. She maintains a personal weapon (the bow, or a collapsible secondary) within arm's reach at rest. She wakes at low-amplitude stimuli. This would be pathological in a librarian; in an active combat operative it is occupational fitness. The DSM allows for criterion E to be present and adaptive, but the threshold for *disorder* requires functional impairment, which the subject does not exhibit. She is, by every observable metric, more functional than her non-traumatized peers.

**Duration.** More than ten years since index trauma, with no documented acute decompensation specifically tied to the assault.

**Functional impairment.** None attributable to the trauma response. The presentation is best characterized as **PTSD in partial remission with successful sublimation**, or — using the post-traumatic growth literature (Tedeschi & Calhoun framework) — as **a textbook PTG case** with high scores in the *personal strength*, *new possibilities*, and *relating to others* domains, moderate scores in *appreciation of life*, and (consistent with her non-religious framing) negligible scores in the *spiritual change* domain.

**Why this is the primary diagnosis rather than "no diagnosis."** The somatic encoding, the startle pattern, the architectural hypervigilance, and the vocational specificity of her response all argue that something *is* still active. To call her asymptomatic would be to confuse successful coping with absence of injury. The injury is present, has been competently metabolized, and continues to shape behavior. The correct framing is *partial remission with growth*, not *recovery without sequelae*.

---

### 1.2 Adjustment-Type Reactions, Recurrent, in the Family-of-Origin Domain (DSM-5-TR 309.x / ICD-11 6B43, recurrent and circumscribed)

The subject exhibits a distinct cluster of brief, situationally-bounded dysregulation episodes tied exclusively to revelations involving her parents — Derek Bishop's criminality, Eleanor Bishop's faked death, Eleanor's villainy, Eleanor's repeated betrayals. Each episode follows a stereotyped course: brief private affective discharge (irritability, withdrawal of usual humor, terse register with intimates), 24–72 hour reorganization phase, return to baseline with organized counter-action.

These episodes do not meet threshold for major depressive episode, do not generalize to other life domains, do not produce occupational impairment lasting beyond the reorganization window, and do not chronify. They are best understood as **recurrent adjustment reactions to acute relational stressors in a specific, predictable, ongoing context** — i.e., to having parents who keep being who they are.

---

## 2. SECONDARY / TRAIT-LEVEL FEATURES (SUBCLINICAL)

These do not meet diagnostic threshold but are clinically meaningful and would be flagged in a comprehensive workup.

### 2.1 Counter-dependent Trait Cluster

Difficulty accepting material help; preference for material deprivation over compromised assistance; chronic under-utilization of available resources (the Bishop fortune, the Avengers logistical apparatus, Stark-level material support that would be available on request). The Los Angeles arc — living out of a car, taking cases for produce, eating expired food — is the high-water mark and demonstrates the trait is *load-bearing* rather than ornamental. Etiology is clear: every adult who offered her resources in childhood either lied about them, used them as control, or had them confiscated by federal investigators. The internal rule is *resources from others are conditional and weaponized; resources I generate are mine.* Trait is ego-syntonic, partially adaptive (it produced the vocational identity), partially maladaptive (it has cost her medical care, sleep, nutrition, and on at least one occasion tactical safety).

### 2.2 Rescuer-Pattern Specialization, Single-Target (Clint Barton)

The subject exhibits a circumscribed caretaking-of-depressive-mentor pattern with one specific person. This is not generalized codependency — she does not rescue serially, does not collect dependents, does not source her self-worth from caretaking writ large. The pattern is targeted. The features include: chronic monitoring of his affect, assumption of logistical labor he is failing to perform (rent, the dog, the apartment, the team), willingness to subordinate tactical positions to his safety beyond what the threat calculus warrants, and a documented inability to leave him to his own consequences when his consequences are clearly his own. The specificity argues this is not a personality structure but a single-relationship adaptation — likely a transferred parental-protective role, given that Clint occupies an explicitly father-adjacent slot and is the one elder who has consistently kept his word. The maladaptation is mild and stable. The risk is drift: if Clint deteriorates further, the subject's tolerance for her own deferred needs is high enough to be self-damaging.

### 2.3 Reality-Testing Lacuna, Single Object (Eleanor Bishop)

The subject's reality-testing is excellent in every domain except one. With her mother, she repeatedly upgrades the trustworthiness estimate on insufficient evidence, gives access she has rationally decided not to give, and is then surprised — narratively, if not psychologically — when betrayed. This is not delusion; it is a circumscribed motivated-reasoning blind spot in the universal-human zone of *the parent one cannot finish writing off.* The pattern has stabilized into a recognizable cycle (re-engagement → wary collaboration → betrayal → recoil → 18–36 month dormancy → re-engagement). The cycle's amplitude has decreased over time as the evidence has accumulated; the cycle has not extinguished. Sub-clinical, but the single most reliable predictor of poor decision-making in the subject's record.

### 2.4 Mild Defended-Sore-Spot Reactivity (Underestimation)

Predictable irritation, accompanied by increased risk tolerance, when condescended to on grounds of age, gender, or wealth. The subject will take a harder shot, accept a higher-risk angle, and stay in a fight longer than necessary to disprove a dismissive read. This is exploitable by a competent adversary and has been exploited in canon. Trait-level, not disorder-level; the kind of thing a treating clinician would name and the subject would acknowledge with a tight grin.

---

## 3. ETIOLOGY

The presentation is comprehensively accounted for by:

1. **Index sexual trauma in mid-adolescence**, in a developmental window where identity is consolidating; the trauma is incorporated into the consolidation rather than disrupting it, producing a self-concept *organized around* the refusal of victim status.
2. **Chronic relational unreliability of biological family** across the entire developmental span: a performatively-present but ethically-compromised father, a mother whose absence was a lie and whose presence was a manipulation, an older sister modeled as vapid and non-protective. This produced the dismissive stance toward bloodline attachment and the high-investment stance toward chosen family.
3. **Class-of-origin dissonance** — wealth from criminal sources, surrounded by performances of legitimacy. This produced the durable suspicion of inheritance, status, and unearned resource.
4. **Early validation by competent strangers** — the Young Avengers cohort, then Steve Rogers' name-bestowal, then Clint Barton's eventual partnership. These events provided the corrective relational experiences that allowed sublimation to succeed where withdrawal might have been the more common outcome. The presence of *witnesses who saw her accurately* in the post-trauma window is, in clinical terms, the single most prognostically favorable variable in her record.

The fact that the trauma response sublimated rather than chronified is best explained by the combination of (a) intact pre-trauma personality structure, (b) immediate access to a credible mastery pathway (training, then team), and (c) the corrective relational input above. Remove any one of these and the clinical picture would likely be substantially worse.

---

## 4. COURSE OVER TIME

**Adolescence (post-trauma to Young Avengers debut).** Acute reorganization phase. Training intensifies; affect is constrained; identity is built deliberately. No documented dissociative or acute-stress episodes in this window, though canonical coverage is thin and absence of evidence is not evidence of absence.

**Young Avengers era (late teens).** Stabilization through team membership. Hypervigilance operationalizes into role. Leadership emerges in vacuums; the subject is functional, occasionally insufferable in the way competent adolescents are, and demonstrably regulated under combat conditions. No psychiatric event of note.

**Transitional period (Dark Reign / Siege-adjacent).** Mild attrition signature — the constant operational tempo plus the dissolution of the Young Avengers' original cohesion produces a brief period of disorganized affiliation. The subject's response is to relocate (Los Angeles) and rebuild rather than to decompensate. This is a critical longitudinal datum: her stress response is *geographic and vocational reorganization*, not symptom production.

**Los Angeles / Fraction-Aja era (early-to-mid twenties).** Voluntary material deprivation; vocational autonomy established; rescuer-pattern with Clint consolidates; severe physical trauma sustained (the Madame Masque beating) and metabolized without subsequent avoidance signature. This is the most observed period and the cleanest evidence for the high-functioning post-traumatic adaptation. Mild loneliness signature, no depressive episode.

**Thompson solo / West Coast Avengers era (mid twenties).** Direct confrontation with the maternal pathology. The recurrent adjustment-reaction cycle is fully visible here. Capacity to lead a roster of severely difficult personalities demonstrates that the trauma-shaped specializations have not narrowed her interpersonal range — she manages chaos, including chaos that resembles her own original family system, without taking on the family system's affect.

**Recent A-list integration.** Increased exposure to peer company at the Captain America / Stark tier. No deference pattern, no impostor signature, no destabilization. The self-concept is robust at this exposure level, which is itself diagnostic of its underlying integrity.

**Projected course.** The trauma-related symptomatology is unlikely to chronify or worsen absent a major destabilizing event. The two specific vulnerabilities — Eleanor and Clint — are the projected sites of any future psychiatric event. A catastrophic loss of Clint, in particular, would likely produce the first sustained depressive episode of the subject's adult life; the rescuer role is load-bearing for the subject in ways she has not metabolized. Eleanor's death, by contrast, would likely produce a brief acute-grief reaction followed by relief and reorganization — the relationship is already mostly mourned.

---

## 5. COMORBIDITY

**Present:** None at diagnostic threshold beyond the partial-remission PTSD and the recurrent narrow-domain adjustment reactions.

**Expected but absent:** The trauma literature would predict elevated lifetime risk for major depressive disorder, generalized anxiety, substance use disorder, and complex PTSD features. The subject exhibits none of these. The protective factors — intact pre-trauma personality, mastery pathway, corrective witnesses, articulated meaning-frame around the trauma — are sufficient to explain the absence, but the absence is genuinely unusual and worth marking.

**Subclinical patterns worth periodic re-assessment:** counter-dependency, single-target rescuer, family-of-origin reality-testing lacuna, underestimation-reactivity. None warrant intervention; all warrant noticing.

---

## 6. DIFFERENTIAL DIAGNOSIS — WHAT SHE IS NOT, AND WHY

This section is where a careful workup earns its keep. The subject's surface presentation — confident, mission-organized, well-armed, family-estranged, mentor-attached, witty under fire — could be misread in several directions by a clinician working from snapshot data. The misreadings are addressed individually.

### 6.1 Not Borderline Personality Disorder

The most common misread of a high-functioning trauma survivor with a turbulent family-of-origin and a knife-edge vocation. The subject meets none of the criteria. Identity is not unstable — it is the *most* stable thing about her, across two decades of canonical record. Relationships are not characterized by idealization/devaluation cycling — her loyalties, once formed by demonstrated reliability, are durable across years and across the relational rupture/repair cycles common to any long peer association, but the *baseline regard* does not oscillate. Abandonment-panic is not present; she has been left, repeatedly, and her response is to reorganize, not to panic. Self-harm is absent. Affective storms are absent — her stress response is *constriction toward task*, not affective escalation. Impulsivity in damaging modalities (substance, sex, spending, risky driving outside operational context) is absent. The single feature that could be misread is the chronic-Eleanor cycle, which superficially resembles an idealization/devaluation pattern. It is not; it is a single-target reality-testing lacuna in a person whose reality-testing is otherwise excellent. The amplitude is too small, the target is too specific, and the pattern is too stable across time to qualify as borderline organization.

### 6.2 Not Major Depressive Disorder, current or recurrent

No anhedonia. No sustained low mood beyond context-appropriate sadness. No self-deprecating cognitive triad. No psychomotor retardation. No sleep architecture consistent with depression (her sleep disruption is hypervigilance-pattern, not depressive-pattern — early waking to stimulus, not early waking to ideation; difficulty falling asleep on operational nights, not anhedonic insomnia). No suicidal ideation in canon. The in-text contrast with Clint Barton — who has all of these features — functions as a control case and is almost certainly authorial. The subject is exposed to identical environmental stressors as Clint and does not develop his symptom profile; the differential variable is pre-existing personality structure and the successful early sublimation of the index trauma.

### 6.3 Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder

Confidence is calibrated to demonstrated competence and accepts correction. The subject shares credit (the Young Avengers, the West Coast roster, Clint), accepts orders when orders are warranted (Steve Rogers in the field, Clint in his areas of specific expertise), tolerates being wrong (and has acknowledged it in canon without affective injury), and exhibits genuine curiosity about other people's interior lives. The grandiose substructure is absent; the vulnerable-narcissistic substructure is absent; envy is not in evidence; entitlement is, if anything, paradoxically *low* given her actual entitlement on every relevant axis. The underestimation-reactivity could be misread as narcissistic injury — it is not; it is a contextually-specific irritation that produces over-functioning, not the affective collapse or rage characteristic of narcissistic wound.

### 6.4 Not Generalized Anxiety Disorder

Planning is task-driven and bounded by the task, not free-floating and unbounded. The subject does not exhibit the cognitive-rumination signature of GAD — she does not worry about generalized futures, does not catastrophize across domains, does not exhibit the somatic anxiety profile (chronic muscle tension undifferentiated from operational readiness, GI symptoms, the global irritability of chronic worry). Her vigilance is *directional* — toward identifiable threats in identifiable contexts — and resolves when the context resolves. She sleeps. She delegates. She closes the file when the case closes.

### 6.5 Not Complex PTSD (ICD-11 6B41)

The differential matters because the family-of-origin chronicity could suggest C-PTSD. The discriminating features argue against: the subject does not exhibit the three additional C-PTSD criteria of (a) affect dysregulation, (b) negative self-concept, and (c) interpersonal disturbance. Affect is regulated. Self-concept is positive and articulated. Interpersonal functioning, in the chosen-kin domain, is excellent. The maternal/paternal pathology was chronic but was not *engulfing* — it ran in parallel to a child who had material privilege, school, social access, and (critically) an older-sister wedding that her self-insertion turned into the gateway to her chosen family. The bloodline pathology cost her trust in bloodline; it did not cost her the developmental scaffolding required for healthy adult attachment. C-PTSD does not fit.

### 6.6 Not ADHD-pattern

The Clint-comparison again clarifies. The subject's PI practice, however shoestring, is *organized*; her cases close; her arrow inventory is maintained; her appointments are kept; her debts are paid in the order they came due. There is no working-memory signature, no executive-function failure outside ordinary fatigue, no hyperfocus/dysregulation cycling. The energy and momentum that could be misread as hyperactivity are simply trained baseline arousal in a young, conditioned operative.

### 6.7 Not Substance Use Disorder, any class

Negligible alcohol use. No documented illicit substance use. No medication-misuse signature. No hangover-as-impairment ever depicted. The contrast with her mentor is again the in-text control. The trauma-relevant point is that she is the rare survivor whose coping never recruited a substance, which is one of the strongest single predictors of her long-term clinical stability.

### 6.8 Not Eating Disorder

Eats badly when broke; eats normally when not; eats well when others cook. No restriction signature, no binge/purge signature, no body-image preoccupation, no exercise-as-compensation pattern (her exercise is vocational and is not in excess of vocational demand).

### 6.9 Not Dissociative Disorder

No documented dissociative episodes, no fugue, no identity alteration. Memory is intact. The vocational compartmentalization (the PI shingle vs. the Avengers field role vs. the Bishop daughter) is *role-fluent* rather than *dissociative* — she carries the same self across all three, with appropriate situational register.

### 6.10 Not Obsessive-Compulsive Disorder or Obsessive-Compulsive Personality

Planning is bounded, not ritualized. Equipment maintenance is occupational, not compulsive (she does not exhibit distress when interrupted, does not require specific sequences). Order-preference is moderate and ego-syntonic; perfectionism is absent (she releases acceptable work, accepts good-enough outcomes, tolerates mess in others). Rigidity is absent — she is, in fact, notably flexible in tactical improvisation, which is the strongest single argument against an OCPD structure.

### 6.11 Not Antisocial spectrum

Despite the criminal family of origin (a known risk factor) and the operational comfort with violence, the subject exhibits unambiguous empathy, durable interpersonal loyalties, intact moral reasoning, restraint of force calibrated to threat, and protectiveness of the vulnerable. She does not deceive instrumentally; her humor is rarely cruel; her aggression is targeted and proportional. The genetic-environmental loading was present and did not express.

### 6.12 Not a "no-disorder, fully healthy" picture

The opposite misread is also possible — to look at the high functioning, the articulated meaning-frame, the chosen family, the vocation, and conclude there is no clinical picture to assess. This would miss the somatic-encoded startle pattern, the architectural hypervigilance, the bounded reality-testing lacuna, the rescuer-specialization, the recurrent narrow-domain adjustment reactions, and the trauma-shaped vocational identity. She is not unmarked; she is *well-organized around the mark.


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: K. E. BISHOP

*A longitudinal catalog of observable tells, micro-behaviors, decision-heuristics, and somatic signatures, indexed by condition. Compiled from twenty years of canonical observation. Granularity at the level a continuous-surveillance file would maintain — gait, breath, hand position, verbal cadence, sequence of operations.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM

### 1.1 Postural and Somatic Baseline

Subject's resting posture is **upright but not rigid** — shoulders down and back, weight slightly forward over the balls of the feet, hips squared. This is trained posture; the archer's stance bleeds into civilian standing. When she leans, she leans against vertical surfaces with the *outside* shoulder (door frames, walls, kitchen counters), keeping her dominant hand and primary line-of-sight unobstructed. She does not sit with her back to entrances. In coffee shops, restaurants, briefing rooms — corner booth, back to the wall, sightline on the door. This is consistent across two decades and never breaks except in the apartments of three specific people (Clint Barton, America Chavez, Lucky-the-dog's couch by transitive trust).

Resting hands: she **fidgets with linear objects** — pens, chopsticks, arrow shafts, the strap of her quiver, the cord of a phone charger. The fidget is rotational, between thumb and first two fingers, the same micro-motion used to nock and seat an arrow. It is a self-soothing repetition of her trained skill. She does not bite nails, does not pick at cuticles, does not pull hair. The hands are kept *useful*.

Eyes scan in a **slow horizontal sweep, left-to-right, every 40–90 seconds** in unfamiliar spaces, more frequent under load. She marks exits within the first thirty seconds of entering any room — an unconscious habit she's described to Clint as "just looking around," which it is not. In familiar spaces (her own apartment, the Hawkeye Investigations office, Clint's building) the sweep collapses to a brief threshold-check on entry, then nothing.

### 1.2 Verbal Baseline

Speech pace: **medium-fast, articulate, syntactically complete sentences even in casual register.** She does not trail off. She does not use placeholder "um" or "uh" at frequencies typical of her age cohort; when she pauses, she pauses cleanly. The pause is itself information — it usually means she has noticed something and is deciding whether to name it.

Register shifts are sharp and intentional. The default mode is **dry, observational, slightly above her interlocutor's altitude** without condescension — she is the smartest person in most rooms and partially manages this by deflecting with humor. With Clint: register drops to colloquial, profane, sibling-band. With Steve Rogers: register tightens, slang strips out, posture squares. With clients of the LA shingle: warm, plain-spoken, slightly slower — deliberate accommodation. With her mother: clipped, ironic, vowels shortened.

Laughs in **two distinct registers**: a short genuine *huh* — exhaled, low, often at her own observation — and a longer social laugh, half a beat too prompt, used as conversational lubricant with people she does not fully trust. The two are distinguishable on first listen once the pattern is keyed.

### 1.3 Habits of the Day

**Wake:** early, 0530–0700, regardless of prior night. Exception is convalescence. The wake is *clean* — no prolonged in-bed phone use, no snooze cycling. Feet on floor inside two minutes of alarm.

**First hour:** coffee (black, made strong; she owns a French press and resents pod machines on principle), then a body inventory — stretching that doubles as a check for new injuries. During the LA period, the inventory was done in the office bathroom because she lived in the office.

**Training:** non-negotiable, daily, even on travel. Minimum: bow-draw repetitions (a hundred draws dry, fifty live if range available), body-weight conditioning, one of the four martial arts on rotation. She has trained in motel parking lots, hotel stairwells, the Avengers' gym at 0400 to avoid company, and once on the deck of a helicarrier. **The training is not optional and is not negotiable; an outside observer who wants to predict her location at 0600 looks for the nearest range or open floor.**

**Arrows:** inventoried nightly. She lays them out, counts, checks tips, restocks the quiver. The ritual is meditative; she does it the way a chef sharpens knives. It is also the most reliable diagnostic of her internal state — when the inventory is rushed or skipped, something is wrong.

**Sleep:** clean and quick onset when conditions permit, 6–7 hours her preferred dose. Sleeps on her side, weapon within reach (bow leaned against the bedframe, or a knife in the nightstand). Does not sleep deeply in unfamiliar environments; will surface fully alert at the click of a door or change in HVAC pitch.

### 1.4 Dress and Grooming

Personal style: **practical-with-a-signature.** Purple recurs as a deliberate choice, an identity-marker she selected and kept. Outside the suit: jeans, layered tops, jackets with internal pockets, boots she can run in. She does not wear footwear she cannot fight in. Heels appear only at events she cannot avoid, and she changes out of them in the car. Jewelry: minimal, never anything that catches on a string. Hair worn shoulder-length-to-long, **tied back the moment work begins** — a hair-tie is on her wrist at all times.

She owns expensive clothing she rarely wears; the wardrobe she actually inhabits is mid-range, functional, and rotates on a small set of items washed often. This is congruent with the rejection-of-Bishop-money posture.

---

## II. UNDER STRESS (SUSTAINED, NON-ACUTE)

### 2.1 Tells

Stress in subject is **subtractive, not additive.** She does not gain symptoms; she loses lightness. Specifically:

- **Humor frequency drops** before any other index. The dry asides thin out; the social laugh disappears entirely. Verbal register tightens toward declarative.
- **Sentence length shortens.** Where calm-Kate uses a relative clause, stressed-Kate uses a period.
- **Sleep contracts** from 6–7 hours to 4–5. She does not complain about this and will deny it if asked.
- **Coffee intake doubles.** The French press becomes a thermos.
- **The arrow inventory becomes obsessive** — recounted twice, sometimes three times. Tips re-checked. New fletching cut.
- **Training time extends.** Hundred draws becomes two hundred. Conditioning adds a second session.
- **Texting cadence to Clint increases** in frequency but decreases in content — short check-ins, "still alive," "you?" The signal is the cadence, not the message.
- **Eating becomes utilitarian.** She forgets meals or eats the same thing for three days running. Pizza, granola bars, whatever is in the fridge. The LA period normalized this; under stress elsewhere it recurs.
- **Apartment/office tidiness inverts.** A normally moderately-organized space becomes *either* compulsively neat (active casework) *or* abandoned-untidy (depressive overlap with Clint-stress); the tidy axis is diagnostic.

### 2.2 Decision Habits Under Sustained Stress

She works the problem in **discrete, sequenced passes**: gather, sort, decide, execute. She resists premature commitment to a hypothesis longer than most operators her age — investigative discipline carries over from the PI work. When stressed, the passes shorten and the gather phase compresses, which is when she makes her characteristic *one* error per arc: usually a misread of an intimate (Eleanor; Clint), almost never a tactical misread.

She **does not ask for help under sustained stress.** This is the most stable counter-dependency signature in the file. The threshold for asking is calibrated against a private internal standard of "have I exhausted what I can do," and the standard is set high. Operationally exploitable.

---

## III. ACUTE THREAT / COMBAT

### 3.1 Pre-Engagement (Seconds to Minutes Before)

- **Breathing slows and deepens.** Diaphragmatic, four-count in, six-count out. Trained. Visible in the rise and fall of the shoulders.
- **Hand drifts to the bow grip** if armed; if unarmed, to the small of the back where a knife or arrow-as-knife would be.
- **Verbal output continues but shifts function** — calm-Kate talks to communicate; pre-fight Kate talks to *anchor and observe*. She narrates what she sees, often as wisecrack. The wisecrack is not bravado; it is a respiration-paced cognitive offload that keeps her arousal in the green zone.
- **Eyes go to the high ground first.** Rooftops, balconies, mezzanines, vents. She is an archer; she thinks vertically.
- **She isolates the most dangerous combatant** within the first three seconds of scan and re-checks that target every 8–12 seconds throughout. Other threats are tracked but downgraded.
- **Stance widens by approximately 15–20%.** Knees soften. Weight forward.

### 3.2 Engagement

Combat behavior is **economical, vertical, and patient.** She does not rush. She moves to angle and elevation. She prefers to engage from cover and from above. When forced into close quarters she fights in the **bow-as-staff / arrow-as-blade** register — Fraction/Aja established this and it has held: the bow doubles as melee tool, the arrow as stabbing implement when quivers run dry.

- **Shot selection:** disabling over killing as a strong default. Legs, hands, shoulder joints, eyes (of vehicles, drones, optics). She does not enjoy killing and does not do it casually; when she does, it is decided in advance and executed without ceremony.
- **Trick-arrow usage:** she has a fluent improvisational relationship with utility arrows but does not over-rely. The plain arrow is her workhorse. She will use a putty arrow or a net arrow as the situation invites; she will not select a gimmick when a clean shot is available.
- **Movement pattern:** runs, vaults, climbs. She uses environment aggressively — fire escapes, parked cars, dumpsters, awnings. She is a parkour-fluent archer; static engagement is her last preference.
- **Talks throughout.** To opponents, to allies, to herself. The patter increases with risk. Cessation of patter is the single most important warning sign that something is very wrong — silent-Kate in a fight means she has been hurt, has identified a kill-decision, or has lost a teammate.
- **Reload discipline is automatic.** Quiver-check between flurries. She knows her arrow count without looking and will call it out to teammates as resource information ("six left, then I'm a stick").

### 3.3 Injury Response

- **Tachy-onset stoicism.** She gets quieter, not louder, when hit. Reports injury *under* its true severity to teammates by approximately 30–40%. "I'm fine" means walking wounded; "it's nothing" means significant; silence means serious.
- **Continues mission past sustainable threshold.** This is the Madame Masque arc's lesson and has not fully been learned; she will fight through concussion, will draw a bow with a fractured rib, will run on a sprained ankle.
- **Self-triage is competent.** Field-dresses her own wounds. Carries basic medical in the quiver-bottom or pack.
- **Refuses extraction unless mission-completed.** Reliable to the point of operational hazard.

### 3.4 Post-Engagement (Minutes After)

- **Adrenaline dump signature:** mild hand tremor, increased thirst, brief verbal *over*-flow — the patter that was tactical becomes social. She talks more, faster, lighter for the first 5–10 minutes after a fight. This is her cleanest tell that the fight is over for her body.
- **Inventories arrows immediately.** Recovers spent shafts when possible. The inventory is restoration ritual as much as resource management.
- **Checks on teammates** before checking on herself. Order: dog, then Clint, then others, then self. Reliable to the point that an adversary tracking her wellbeing should watch the others first.
- **Eats.** Within thirty minutes of fight end, if food is available. Carbs, salty, fast. Pizza is the canonical post-fight food.

---

## IV. INTIMACY (NON-ROMANTIC AND ROMANTIC)

### 4.1 With Chosen Family (America Chavez, Cassie Lang, the Young Avengers cohort, Lucky, Clint)

- **Physical contact threshold is low and warm.** She initiates hugs, leans into shoulders, sits close on couches, takes the dog into her lap. The body-contact is non-erotic and high-frequency with this small circle and almost nonexistent outside it.
- **Verbal register: profane, fast, affectionate, teasing.** She insults the people she loves; the insult is the love-language. Tone-deafness to this register is a reliable disqualifier in her circle.
- **Listens with full body.** Faces the speaker, phone face-down. Does not multitask intimacy.
- **Remembers operational detail about her people** — anniversaries of losses, allergies, dog's medication schedule, Clint's hearing-aid battery cycle. She files this without being asked and acts on it without being thanked.
- **Defends them disproportionately.** A slight directed at America or Cassie produces faster and harder response than a slight directed at Kate herself. This is one of the clearest exploitable patterns in the file.

### 4.2 With Clint Specifically

The relationship is its own register. **Sibling-band with reverse-parentification overlay.**

- Lets herself in. Feeds the dog. Throws out the takeout containers. Checks the fridge. Restocks coffee.
- **Reads his mood inside ten seconds** of seeing him and adjusts her own register accordingly — louder if he is sinking, quieter if he is wired.
- **Holds the bow line he drops** without commenting on the drop. Tactical and emotional cover for him; he knows and she knows and they do not discuss.
- Sleeps on his couch without invitation when she has decided he should not be alone. Will fight him about this.
- **Will not let an outsider criticize him in her presence.** Even when she agrees with the criticism.
- The single relationship most likely to make her bend her own rules.

### 4.3 Romantic

- **Initiation is reciprocal, not pursuing.** She responds; she does not chase. The exception (Noh-Varr / Marvel Boy) is light flirtation rather than pursuit.
- **Sleeps with the lights low but not off.** Hypervigilance carve-out.
- **Does not introduce partners to chosen family quickly.** The reverse threshold is high; the chosen-family veto is real even if unspoken.
- **Disengages cleanly when disengaging.** No prolonged ambiguity, no breadcrumbing. Eli Bradley's relationship ended without drama and they continued to coexist on teams.
- **Does not source self-worth from partners.** A partner who attempts to become load-bearing for her identity will find no purchase. Likely a deal-breaker.

### 4.4 With Mentors and Authority

- **Eye contact steady; chin neutral; no submissive lowering.**
- **Will interrupt to correct factual error.** Has done so to Steve Rogers, to her father, to senior Avengers. The interruption is polite, brief, and final.
- **Does not seek approval beyond a single confirming glance.** When she gets the glance, she moves on. When she does not get it, she does not press.
- **Calls senior figures by first name** as soon as social permission is granted, and treats the granting as routine. She is not impressed by titles.

---

## V. GRIEF

### 5.1 Acute Grief (loss of a teammate, of Lucky's near-death, of a betrayed-by-Eleanor revelation)

- **Brief private dysregulation, geographically isolated.** She withdraws to a bathroom, a stairwell, a rooftop, the office at night. Cries quickly, quietly, alone, and not for long — minutes, not hours. The crying is followed by a face-wash and a return.
- **Does not announce the grief.** Teammates often learn after.
- **Re-emerges with work.** Grief is metabolized through task — a case, a training session, a hunt for the person responsible.
- **Touch tolerance increases briefly** with the inner circle. She will let America hold her. She will let Clint sit next to her in silence. She rarely asks for this; she accepts it when offered.

### 5.2 Sustained Grief

- **Sleep further contracts; arrow inventory becomes more elaborate; humor returns last.**
- **Anniversaries marked privately.** She remembers dates. She does not announce that she remembers.
- **Does not develop substance pattern.** Will drink a beer with Clint on the anniversary of a loss; will not get drunk.
- **Re-engages with the world through a small kind action** — adopting another stray, taking a pro-bono case, calling Cassie for no reason. The kind action is her tell that she has cleared the worst of it.

---

## VI. VICTORY

### 6.1 Tactical Victory (Mission Complete)

- **Understated.** A nod, a one-line wisecrack, a fist-bump. She does not gloat, does not pose, does not monologue.
- **Credits the team aloud.** Names them. Specifically. "America did the heavy lifting, I just shot the thing." She is reliable about this to the point that an absence of credit-sharing is itself a tell — usually meaning she is exhausted or hurt.
- **Buys the food.** Post-mission meals are her treat when she has money; when she doesn't, she organizes the order and pays whoever fronts it back later, on schedule.
- **Calls her people.** America gets a check-in; Cassie gets a text; Clint gets a visit.

### 6.2 Personal Victory (Confronted Eleanor; Closed the LA office on a case she cared about; Bested a doubter)

- **Quiet satisfaction, often invisible to onlookers.** A small private smile. A loosening of the shoulders. She does not announce.
- **Does not rest on it.** Moves to the next task within hours.
- **Records it privately.** Likely keeps a case-log; the PI shingle was organized enough to suggest a paper trail.

### 6.3 Recognition / Public Honors

- **Visibly uncomfortable with ceremony.** Will accept on behalf of the team, deflects to others, gets off the stage quickly.
- **Will not wear formal recognition pieces** outside the moment of bestowal. The Captain America bow-bestowal is the singular exception, and the bow itself is *worked*, not curated. She does not preserve the relic; she uses the tool.

---

## VII. DEFEAT

### 7.1 Tactical Defeat

- **After-action review, alone first, then with team.** She reconstructs the engagement step by step, identifies her own errors first, then the team's. Allocates blame *to herself* at a slightly higher rate than the evidence supports — a mild over-correction consistent with leadership conscientiousness.
- **Does not externalize.** Will not blame equipment, weather, intel failure, or teammates in the first pass even when warranted. Will adjust in subsequent passes.
- **Returns to training within 24 hours.** Repetitions of the specific skill that failed. If the failed shot was at distance, the next day's session is distance work.
- **Does not retreat from leadership.** Conspicuous: a defeated Kate is not a withdrawn Kate. She doubles into the role.

### 7.2 Personal Defeat (Eleanor manipulating her again; failing a client; Clint relapsing into a worse state)

- **Brief withdrawal, 12–48 hours.** Phone unanswered or terse. Then return.
- **The Eleanor-zone defeats produce the only behavior approaching denial in the file** — she will minimize the latest betrayal in the first day, then reorganize toward realism by day three. The cycle is repeatable and predictable.
- **The Clint-zone defeats produce the protective overdrive** — extended overnight presence at his apartment, cancelling her own commitments, putting cases on hold.

### 7.3 Existential Defeat (Father confirmed villain; Mother confirmed villain; Young Avengers fracturing)

- **No collapse documented.** Across every such event in canon, she has reorganized inside a week.
- **Doubles down on the chosen-family architecture** — recruits more aggressively, calls her people more often, founds teams (West Coast Avengers post-Eleanor).
- **Does not lose the central narrative.** *I was hurt, I refused to stay hurt, I built this on my own terms* survives every external shock. This is her most durable asset and the single hardest thing about her to break.

---

## VIII. SOCIAL MICROBEHAVIOR / NEGOTIATION

- **Opens warm, settles cool.** First-meeting register is friendlier than working register; she down-shifts as she takes a person's measure. The shift is the assessment.
- **Names everyone.** Coffee-shop baristas, building doormen, clients' kids. Uses names back. Operational and characterological.
- **Tips well.** Service workers consistently receive disproportionate generosity. Vocational respect; also rejection-of-Bishop-class-instinct expressed as inversion.
- **Negotiates from data, not affect.** Will not raise her voice in a price negotiation, in a job pitch, in a confrontation with an institution. Quotes the numbers, waits.
- **Lies poorly to people she likes; lies competently to adversaries.** The investigative undercover work is functional; the personal-life evasion is transparent within her circle and she knows it.

---

## IX. SOLITUDE

- **Tolerates it well.** The LA period demonstrated months of effective solo function.
- **Talks to the dog.** Talks to herself. The internal monologue externalizes when alone, in a low conversational tone — narrating tasks, debating choices.
- **Listens to music while working a case.** Has musical taste; uses it as cognitive scaffolding.
- **Reads.** Case files, novels, the occasional history. She is more literate than she displays; the displayed register is below her actual range, a deliberate choice.
- **Does not isolate as avoidance.** Solitude is restorative, not defensive. Distinguishable from withdrawal by the cleanliness of the space and the maintenance of routine.

---

## X. THE CONSISTENCY ACROSS TWENTY YEARS

The single most striking property of this behavioral atlas is its **temporal stability.** Subject's tells at sixteen (Young Avengers #1, pushing into the wedding crisis with an unfamiliar weapon) are the same tells at her present age: forward weight, scan-the-room, narrate-the-fight, credit-the-team, inventory-the-arrows, check-on-Clint, eat-the-pizza, do-not-ask-for-help. The behavioral structure was set early — by trauma, by training, by the deliberate choice to be a specific person — and has been refined rather than rebuilt.

This is the behavioral signature of someone who **decided who she was going to be before most people get the chance to**, and then spent the next decade and a half being exactly that, with discipline, with humor, and with a small, well-


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — KATE BISHOP
## Section 7: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

*What a week of surveillance would record. Compiled from longitudinal observation; cross-referenced against Fraction/Aja* Hawkeye *(2012–15), Thompson* Hawkeye *(2016–18),* West Coast Avengers *(2018–19), and incidental observation across Young Avengers / Avengers appearances.*

---

### 7.1 The Shape of a Day

Subject is a **morning-anchored, late-night-tolerant** operator. Wakes between 06:40 and 07:30 without an alarm on most days; the body has been trained to it by years of pre-work range time. On nights following case-work that ran past 02:00, she will sleep until 09:00 but not later — she dislikes the disorientation of waking to a sun already high, and has said as much (to Clint, to America, to Ramone) more than once. The phrase she uses is "I lose the day." Surveillance would record her saying it roughly once every three weeks.

First fifteen minutes of consciousness are non-verbal. She does not check her phone in bed; she has a stated rule against it, originating (per a throwaway line in Thompson's run) from her early twenties when she "spent six months waking up to my mother." She sits up, drinks water from a glass left on the nightstand the night before — a fixed ritual, the glass is *always* there, and the absence of one is a tell that the previous night ended badly — then puts her feet on the floor and rolls her right ankle eight times, left ankle eight times. The ankle work is residual from a jiu-jitsu injury never explicitly named in canon but implied by her warm-up patterns in the LA arc.

She showers before coffee. This is unusual and worth noting: most operators reverse this. She has said the shower is "where I figure out the day." A surveillance auditor would clock the showers at six to nine minutes, water-hot, with the bathroom door left ajar — a habit from living alone with a dog that needs access. She washes her hair every other day, no more; the hair is long enough that a daily wash would cost her time she will not give.

Coffee is made in a French press when she is settled and from a Mr. Coffee carafe when she is in motion. She does not buy espresso machines because she breaks them. (Two are accounted for across the Venice arcs; one is referenced by Ramone as having "exploded.") She takes it black at home and with milk in public. The public-milk thing is social camouflage — black coffee invites comment; milky coffee does not. She is aware of this and has used the same logic to order food she doesn't want at stakeouts.

Breakfast is functional and small. Toast, sometimes an egg, frequently nothing. In the LA broke era she ate cereal dry from the box at the kitchen counter. In the better-funded periods she has bagels delivered, splits them with Lucky (the cream cheese half is hers, the everything-bagel crust is his), and reads on her phone with her feet pulled up onto the chair.

---

### 7.2 The Workspace and the Workday

**Hawkeye Investigations** is the spine of her professional week. The office (per Thompson's run, Venice Beach, above a noodle place) is also where she sometimes sleeps when a case is hot. The space is **organized to a degree that surprises people on first visit** — clients expect a noir mess, find a clean desk, color-coded case files (manila for active, green for closed, red for "won't take payment from"), a wall of bow-related equipment hung on pegboard the way a chef hangs knives, and a couch with a folded blanket squared at the foot like a hotel.

Surveillance would record her arriving at the office between 09:00 and 09:45 on a normal weekday, **Lucky preceding her by half a step** (he knows the route; he uses the door before she does). She unlocks with her left hand, holds coffee in her right, and *always glances once at the rooftop opposite before stepping inside.* This is a security tic so habituated she does not know she does it. A trained eye reads it instantly.

Office hours are nominally 10–6. In practice:

- **10:00–11:30** — administrative. Invoices, intake calls, correspondence with the small network of allies who throw her work (a referral pipeline includes a tenants' rights lawyer, two beat cops who like her, a bail bondsman, and at least one ex-client turned permanent friend). She returns calls in batches, never one-off. She writes longhand notes during phone calls — a yellow legal pad, blue pen, very legible printing, never cursive.
- **11:30–13:00** — field. Surveillance, interviews, document pickups. She prefers to do legwork before lunch because "people lie worse when they're hungry" — actual quote, Thompson run.
- **13:00–14:00** — lunch, almost always *out*, almost always *cheap*, almost always *the same three or four places* in rotation. She over-tips when she has it and under-orders when she doesn't. She eats alone with a book or with Clint or America when they're in town. She does not do business lunches; clients meet her at the office.
- **14:00–17:30** — the heavier work: case-building, surveillance write-ups, range time if a case is dormant.
- **17:30–18:30** — gym or range or both.

She does not work nights as a default. Night work is for hot cases or for Avengers business. The boundary is deliberate and was hard-won — a Fraction-era throwaway has her saying, roughly, that if she works every night she becomes Clint, and there can only be one of those.

---

### 7.3 Training — The Non-Negotiable Block

Six days a week, ninety minutes minimum, more if she has the day. **The training is not optional and a week of surveillance would show zero exceptions absent injury or Avengers-level emergency.** This is the most rigidly held appointment in her life, more than any client, meal, or relationship.

Rotation (approximate):

- **Monday — archery, distance.** Outdoor range when LA weather permits. Two hundred arrows minimum, three hundred typical. She shoots both standard recurve and her compound. She does not film herself; she does not use sights for the first hour. The first thirty arrows are slow-draw, eyes-closed-on-release work — she is training the proprioceptive memory, not the visual.
- **Tuesday — striking.** Kickboxing, a gym she has used long enough that the owner doesn't charge her properly. She spars with men twenty pounds heavier than she is by preference. She does not flinch on contact and the gym has stopped trying to pair her with women her weight because she requested otherwise.
- **Wednesday — grappling.** Brazilian jiu-jitsu. She rolls hard, taps cleanly, and is one of those students who is universally liked because she does not ego-spar. She is a purple belt by Thompson-era timeline inference; functionally brown-belt skilled but has never tested.
- **Thursday — archery, trick / movement.** Shooting from motion, from cover, with the off hand, around obstacles, with deliberately handicapped equipment. This is the **Clint inheritance** — trick shots are the part of the craft she keeps because he keeps it, and because the day a perfect-line shot is impossible is the day she'll need this.
